				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Corp.">Oracle Corp.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt"> 

</p>
<p><b>Oracle Corporation</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> computer <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology corporation</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Redwood_Shores,_California" title="Redwood Shores, California">Redwood Shores, California</a>. The company sells <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database software and technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud engineered systems,</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_software" title="Enterprise software">enterprise software</a> products—particularly <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">its own brands of database management systems</a>. In 2019, Oracle was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_software_companies" title="List of the largest software companies">second-largest software company</a> by revenue and market capitalization.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Oracle <p>The company also develops and builds tools for <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> development and systems of middle-tier software, <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="Enterprise resource planning">enterprise resource planning</a> (ERP) software, <a href="/wiki/Human_Capital_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Capital Management">Human Capital Management</a> (HCM) software, <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a> (CRM) software, and <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a> (SCM) software.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p><a href="/wiki/Larry_Ellison" title="Larry Ellison">Larry Ellison</a> co-founded Oracle Corporation in 1977 with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Miner" title="Bob Miner">Bob Miner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Oates" title="Ed Oates">Ed Oates</a> under the name <b>Software Development Laboratories</b> (<b>SDL</b>).<sup id="cite_ref-founders_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-founders-2">[2]</a></sup> Ellison took inspiration<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> from the 1970 paper written by <a href="/wiki/Edgar_F._Codd" title="Edgar F. Codd">Edgar F. Codd</a> on relational database management systems (<a href="/wiki/Relational_database_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Relational database management system">RDBMS</a>) named "A Relational Model of Data for Large Shared Data Banks".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He heard about the <a href="/wiki/IBM_System_R" title="IBM System R">IBM System R</a> database from an article in the <i>IBM Research Journal</i> provided by Oates. Ellison wanted to make Oracle's product compatible with System R, but failed to do so as IBM kept the error codes for their DBMS a secret. SDL changed its name to <b>Relational Software, Inc</b> (<b>RSI</b>) in 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-niemiec_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-niemiec-9">[9]</a></sup> then again to <b>Oracle Systems Corporation</b> in 1983,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> to align itself more closely with its flagship product <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>. At this stage Bob Miner served as the company's senior programmer. On March 12, 1986, the company had its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1995, Oracle Systems Corporation changed its name to <b>Oracle Corporation</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> officially named Oracle, but sometimes referred to as Oracle Corporation, the name of the holding company.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Part of Oracle Corporation's early success arose from using the <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C programming language</a> to implement its products. This eased porting to different <a href="/wiki/Operating_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Operating systems">operating systems</a> most of which support C.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">

</td></tr></tbody></table><p>Oracle ranked No. 82 in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> According to Bloomberg, Oracle's CEO-to-employee pay ratio is 1,205:1. The CEO's compensation in 2017 was $108,295,023. Oracle is one of the approved employers of <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Chartered_Certified_Accountants" title="Association of Chartered Certified Accountants">ACCA</a> and the median employee compensation rate was $89,887.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Products and services" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Oracle designs, manufactures, and sells both software and hardware products, as well as offering services that complement them (such as financing, training, consulting, and hosting services). Many of the products have been added to Oracle's portfolio through <a href="/wiki/List_of_acquisitions_by_Oracle" title="List of acquisitions by Oracle">acquisitions</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Software" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Oracle's E-delivery service (Oracle Software Delivery Cloud) provides generic downloadable Oracle software and documentation.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Databases">Databases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Databases" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>
<ul><li>Release 10: In 2004, Oracle Corporation shipped release 10<i>g</i> (<i>g</i> standing for "grid") as the then latest version of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>. (<a href="/wiki/Oracle_Application_Server" title="Oracle Application Server">Oracle Application Server</a> 10<i>g</i> using <a href="/wiki/Java_EE" class="mw-redirect" title="Java EE">Java EE</a> integrated with the server part of that version of the database, making it possible to deploy <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">web</a>-technology applications. The application server comprised the first <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Three-tier (computing)">middle-tier</a> software designed for <a href="/wiki/Grid_computing" title="Grid computing">grid computing</a>. The interrelationship between <a href="/wiki/Grid_computing" title="Grid computing">Oracle</a> 10<i>g</i> and <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> allowed developers to set up <a href="/wiki/Stored_procedure" title="Stored procedure">stored procedures</a> written in the Java language, as well as those written in the traditional Oracle database programming language, <a href="/wiki/PL/SQL" title="PL/SQL">PL/SQL</a>.)</li>
<li>Release 11: Release 11g became available in 2007. Oracle Corporation released Oracle Database 11g Release 2 in September 2009. This version was available in four commercial editions—Enterprise Edition, Standard Edition, Standard Edition One, and Personal Edition—and in one free edition—the Express Edition. The licensing of these editions shows various restrictions and obligations that were called complex by licensing expert Freirich Florea.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The Enterprise Edition (DB EE), the most expensive of the Database Editions, has the fewest restrictions—but nevertheless has complex licensing. Oracle Corporation constrains the Standard Edition (DB SE) and Standard Edition One (SE1) with more licensing restrictions, in accordance with their lower price.</li>
<li>Release 12: Release 12<i>c</i> (<i>c</i> standing for "cloud") became available on July 1, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul><p>Oracle Corporation has acquired and developed the following additional database technologies:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Berkeley_DB" title="Berkeley DB">Berkeley DB</a>, which offers <a href="/wiki/Embedded_database" title="Embedded database">embedded database</a> processing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Rdb" title="Oracle Rdb">Oracle Rdb</a>, a relational database system running on <a href="/wiki/OpenVMS" title="OpenVMS">OpenVMS</a> platforms. Oracle acquired Rdb in 1994 from <a href="/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation" title="Digital Equipment Corporation">Digital Equipment Corporation</a>. Oracle has since made many enhancements to this product and development continues as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TimesTen" title="TimesTen">TimesTen</a>, which features in-memory database operations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Essbase" title="Essbase">Oracle Essbase</a>, which continues the <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_Solutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperion Solutions">Hyperion</a> Essbase tradition of <a href="/wiki/Multidimensional_database" class="mw-redirect" title="Multidimensional database">multi-dimensional database</a> management</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, a relational database management system licensed under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a>, initially developed by <a href="/wiki/MySQL_AB" title="MySQL AB">MySQL AB</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_NoSQL_Database" title="Oracle NoSQL Database">Oracle NoSQL Database</a>, a scalable, distributed key-value <a href="/wiki/NoSQL" title="NoSQL">NoSQL</a> database<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li></ul><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Middleware">Middleware</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Middleware" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Fusion_Middleware" title="Oracle Fusion Middleware">Oracle Fusion Middleware</a></div>
<p>Oracle Fusion Middleware is a family of <a href="/wiki/Middleware" title="Middleware">middleware</a> software products, including (for instance) <a href="/wiki/Application_server" title="Application server">application server</a>, <a href="/wiki/System_integration" title="System integration">system integration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_process_management" title="Business process management">business process management</a> (BPM), user interaction, <a href="/wiki/Content_management" title="Content management">content management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Identity_management" title="Identity management">identity management</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a> (BI) products.
</p>
<h5 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oracle_Secure_Enterprise_Search">Oracle Secure Enterprise Search</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Oracle Secure Enterprise Search" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h5>
<p>Oracle Secure Enterprise Search (SES), Oracle's <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_search" title="Enterprise search">enterprise-search</a> offering, gives users the ability to search for content across multiple locations, including websites, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> files, file servers, <a href="/wiki/Content_management_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Content management systems">content management systems</a>, enterprise resource planning systems, <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a> systems, and databases.
</p>
<h5 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oracle_Beehive">Oracle Beehive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Oracle Beehive" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Beehive" title="Oracle Beehive">Oracle Beehive</a></div>
<p>Released in 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Beehive" title="Oracle Beehive">Oracle Beehive</a> <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Collaboration software">collaboration software</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Team" title="Team">team</a> workspaces (including <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wikis</a>, team calendaring and file sharing), email, calendar, instant messaging, and conferencing on a single platform. Customers can use Beehive as licensed software or as <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> ("SaaS").<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Applications" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Oracle also sells a suite of <a href="/wiki/Business_application" class="mw-redirect" title="Business application">business applications</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Oracle_E-Business_Suite" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle E-Business Suite">Oracle E-Business Suite</a> includes software to perform various enterprise functions related to (for instance) financials, manufacturing, <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a> (CRM), <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="Enterprise resource planning">enterprise resource planning</a> (ERP) and <a href="/wiki/Human_Resource_Management_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Resource Management Systems">human resource management</a>.  The Oracle Retail Suite<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
covers the retail-industry <a href="/wiki/Vertical_market" title="Vertical market">vertical</a>, providing merchandise management, price management, invoice matching, allocations, store operations management, warehouse management, demand forecasting, merchandise financial planning, assortment planning, and category management.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Users can access these facilities through a browser interface over the Internet or via a corporate intranet.
</p><p>Following a number of acquisitions beginning in 2003, especially in the area of applications, Oracle Corporation as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> maintains a number of product lines:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Fusion_Applications" title="Oracle Fusion Applications">Oracle Fusion Applications</a></li>
<li>Oracle Social Engagement and Monitoring (SEM) System – Oracle has developed a Social Engagement and Monitoring Cloud service that allows <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">businesses</a> to capture relevant brand conversation from global web and social channels to understand commentary on their products. The Social Engagement and Monitoring cloud provides the most effective and efficient responses across social and customer experience channels. SEM is able to route correct responses to the right team, member, or customer-experience channel to ensure the best customer service. The analysis helps vendors to understand what is important to customers. It identifies trends, spikes, and anomalies to make real-time course corrections. It also can identify brand advocates. The SEM cloud identifies customer intention and interests by analyzing the common ways customers talk about a product or a service.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (August 2016)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_E-Business_Suite" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle E-Business Suite">Oracle E-Business Suite</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PeopleSoft" title="PeopleSoft">PeopleSoft Enterprise</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siebel_Systems" title="Siebel Systems">Siebel</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JD_Edwards" title="JD Edwards">JD Edwards</a>
<ul><li>JD Edwards EnterpriseOne</li>
<li>JD Edwards World</li></ul></li>
<li>Merchandise Operations Management (Formerly Retek)</li>
<li>Planning &amp; Optimisation</li>
<li>Store Operations (Formerly 360Commerce)</li></ul><p>Development of applications commonly takes place in Java (using <a href="/wiki/Oracle_JDeveloper" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle JDeveloper">Oracle JDeveloper</a>) or through PL/SQL (using, for example, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Forms" title="Oracle Forms">Oracle Forms</a> and Oracle Reports/BIPublisher).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Oracle Corporation has started<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> a drive toward "wizard"-driven environments with a view to enabling non-programmers to produce simple data-driven applications.
</p>
<h5 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Third-party_applications">Third-party applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Third-party applications" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h5>
<p>Oracle Corporation works with "Oracle Certified Partners" to enhance its overall product marketing. The variety of applications from third-party vendors includes <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> applications for archiving, splitting and control, <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="Enterprise resource planning">ERP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">CRM</a> systems, as well as more niche and focused products providing a range of commercial functions in areas like <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a>, financial control and <a href="/wiki/Governance,_risk_management,_and_compliance" title="Governance, risk management, and compliance">governance, risk management, and compliance</a> (GRC). Vendors include <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, Creoal Consulting, UC4 Software,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Motus,_LLC" title="Motus, LLC">Motus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Knoa_Software" title="Knoa Software">Knoa Software</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Enterprise_management">Enterprise management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Enterprise management" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Enterprise_Manager" title="Oracle Enterprise Manager">Oracle Enterprise Manager</a></div>
<p>Oracle Enterprise Manager (OEM) provides web-based monitoring and management tools for Oracle products (and for some third-party software), including database management, middleware management, application management, hardware and virtualization management and cloud management.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Primavera_(software)" title="Primavera (software)">Primavera</a> products of Oracle's Construction &amp; Engineering Global Business Unit (CEGBU) consist of <a href="/wiki/Project_management" title="Project management">project-management</a> software.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_software">Development software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Development software" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Oracle Corporation's tools for developing applications include (among others):
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Designer" title="Oracle Designer">Oracle Designer</a> – a <a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_software_engineering" title="Computer-aided software engineering">CASE</a> tool which integrates with Oracle Developer Suite</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Developer_Suite" title="Oracle Developer Suite">Oracle Developer</a> – which consists of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Forms" title="Oracle Forms">Oracle Forms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Discoverer" title="Oracle Discoverer">Oracle Discoverer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Reports" title="Oracle Reports">Oracle Reports</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_JDeveloper" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle JDeveloper">Oracle JDeveloper</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Freeware" title="Freeware">freeware</a> <a href="/wiki/Integrated_development_environment" title="Integrated development environment">IDE</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NetBeans" title="NetBeans">NetBeans</a>, a Java-based software-development platform</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Application_Express" title="Oracle Application Express">Oracle Application Express</a> – also known as APEX; for web-oriented development</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_SQL_Developer" title="Oracle SQL Developer">Oracle SQL Developer</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Integrated_development_environment" title="Integrated development environment">integrated development environment</a> for working with SQL-based databases</li>
<li>Oracle SQL*Plus Worksheet, a component of Oracle Enterprise Manager (OEM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OEPE" class="mw-redirect" title="OEPE">OEPE</a>, Oracle Enterprise Pack for <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Java_Development_Kit" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Java Development Kit">Open Java Development Kit</a></li>
<li>Oracle Developer Studio – a software generation system for the development of C, C++, Fortran, and Java software</li></ul><p>Many external and third-party tools make the Oracle <a href="/wiki/Database_administrator" title="Database administrator">database administrator</a>'s tasks easier.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="File_systems">File systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: File systems" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ZFS" title="ZFS">ZFS</a> combines <a href="/wiki/File-system" class="mw-redirect" title="File-system">file-system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logical_volume_management" title="Logical volume management">logical volume management</a> functionality.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BtrFS" class="mw-redirect" title="BtrFS">BtrFS</a> "B-tree File-System" is meant to be an improvement over the existing <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> <a href="/wiki/Ext4" title="Ext4">ext4</a> filesystem, and offer features approaching those of <a href="/wiki/ZFS" title="ZFS">ZFS</a>.</li></ul><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_systems">Operating systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Operating systems" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Oracle Corporation develops and supports two operating systems: <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Solaris" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Solaris">Oracle Solaris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Linux" title="Oracle Linux">Oracle Linux</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware">Hardware</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hardware" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OracleExadataExalogic.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/OracleExadataExalogic.JPG/220px-OracleExadataExalogic.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 332px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/OracleExadataExalogic.JPG/220px-OracleExadataExalogic.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="332" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OracleExadataExalogic.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oracle Exadata and Exalogic</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The Sun hardware range acquired by Oracle Corporation's purchase of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_SPARC_T-series_servers" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle SPARC T-series servers">Oracle SPARC T-series servers</a> and M-series <a href="/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">mainframes</a> developed and released after Sun acquisition</li>
<li>Engineered systems: pre-engineered and pre-assembled hardware/software bundles for enterprise use
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Exadata" title="Oracle Exadata">Exadata Database Machine</a> – hardware/software integrated storage<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Exalogic" title="Oracle Exalogic">Exalogic Elastic Cloud</a> – hardware/software integrated application server</li>
<li>Exalytics In-Memory Machine – hardware/software integrated in-memory analytics server<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oracle Database Appliance<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Big_Data_Appliance" title="Oracle Big Data Appliance">Big Data Appliance</a> – integrated map-reduce/<a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a> solution<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>SPARC SuperCluster T4-4 – a general purpose engineered system<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Services" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oracle_Cloud">Oracle Cloud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Oracle Cloud" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Cloud" title="Oracle Cloud">Oracle Cloud</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> service offered by Oracle Corporation providing servers, storage, network, applications and services through a global network of Oracle Corporation managed <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a>. The company allows these services to be <a href="/wiki/Provisioning" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisioning">provisioned</a> on demand over the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>Oracle Cloud provides <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_service" title="Infrastructure as a service">Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">Platform as a Service (PaaS)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">Software as a Service (SaaS)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Data_as_a_service" title="Data as a service">Data as a Service (DaaS)</a>. These services are used to build, deploy, integrate and extend applications in the cloud. This platform supports <a href="/wiki/Open_standard" title="Open standard">open standards</a> (<a href="/wiki/SQL" title="SQL">SQL</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Representational_state_transfer" title="Representational state transfer">REST</a>, etc.) open-source solutions (<a href="/wiki/Kubernetes" title="Kubernetes">Kubernetes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apache_Hadoop" title="Apache Hadoop">Hadoop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apache_Kafka" title="Apache Kafka">Kafka</a>, etc.) and a variety of <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a>, tools and <a href="/wiki/Software_framework" title="Software framework">frameworks</a> including Oracle-specific, <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">Open Source</a> and <a href="/wiki/Third-party_software_component" title="Third-party software component">third-party software</a> and systems.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Software as a Service">Software as a Service</a> (SaaS)<sup id="cite_ref-oracle_cloud_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle_cloud-37">[37]</a></sup><ul><li>Enterprise applications: <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">SCM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_performance_management" title="Enterprise performance management">EPM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_Capital_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Capital Management">HCM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Enterprise_Resource_Planning_Cloud" title="Oracle Enterprise Resource Planning Cloud">ERP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customer_experience" title="Customer experience">CX</a> SaaS offerings<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Platform as a Service">Platform as a Service</a> (PaaS)<sup id="cite_ref-oracle_cloud_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle_cloud-37">[37]</a></sup><ul><li>Oracle has branded its Platform as a Service as <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Cloud_Platform" title="Oracle Cloud Platform">Oracle Cloud Platform</a>.  Oracle Cloud Platform include Data Management, Application Development, Integration, Content and Experience, Business Analytics, Management and Security.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Platform services on which to build and deploy applications or extend SaaS applications: database, Java application server, mobile, business analytics, integration, process, big data, <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_Things" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet of Things">Internet of Things</a>, <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a> etc.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Infrastructure as a Service">Infrastructure as a Service</a> (IaaS)<sup id="cite_ref-oracle_cloud_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle_cloud-37">[37]</a></sup><ul><li>Oracle has branded its Infrastructure as a Service as  Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (OCI). Oracle Cloud Infrastructure offerings include the following services.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><ul><li>Compute Service</li>
<li>Storage Service</li>
<li>Network Service</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul><p>On July 28, 2016 Oracle bought <a href="/wiki/NetSuite" title="NetSuite">NetSuite</a>, the very first cloud company, for $9.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On May 16, 2018 Oracle announced that it had acquired DataScience.com, a privately held cloud workspace platform for data science projects and workloads.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_services">Other services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other services" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<ul><li>Oracle Consulting – technical and business expert services</li>
<li>Oracle Financing</li>
<li>Oracle Support
<ul><li>Product support: Oracle Corporation identifies its customers and their support entitlements using CSI (Customer Support Identifier) codes.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Registered customers can submit <a href="/wiki/Service_request_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Service request management">Service Requests</a> (SRs)<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>—usually via the web-accessible My Oracle Support<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> (MOS),<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> a re-incarnation of Oracle Metalink<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> with web access administered by a site Customer User Administrator (CUA).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>Critical Patch Updates: since 2005 Oracle Corporation has grouped collections of <a href="/wiki/Patch_(computing)" title="Patch (computing)">patches</a> and security fixes for its products each quarter into a "Critical Patch Update" (CPU), released each January, April, July and October.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oracle Configuration Manager (OCM, previously Customer Configuration repository or CCR) gathers and uploads details of the configuration of Oracle software.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oracle Auto Service Request (ASR) automatically creates Service Requests for specific hardware faults on qualified Oracle server, storage, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Exadata" title="Oracle Exadata">Oracle Exadata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Exalogic" title="Oracle Exalogic">Oracle Exalogic</a> products.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>My Oracle Support Community (MOSC)<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>Oracle University (training in Oracle products)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oracle_Certification_Program" title="Oracle Certification Program">Oracle Certification Program</a></li></ul></li>
<li>NetSuite Social Impact program assists nonprofits with moving operations to the cloud.  In October 2018, Oracle announced the expansion of the program to include product donation, pro bono expansion and online community building.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Marketing" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_practices">Sales practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sales practices" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1990, Oracle laid off 10% (about 400 people) of its work force because of accounting errors.<sup id="cite_ref-zdnet200620_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet200620-57">[57]</a></sup> This crisis came about because of Oracle's "up-front" marketing strategy, in which sales people urged potential customers to buy the largest possible amount of software all at once. The sales people then booked the value of future license sales in the current quarter, thereby increasing their bonuses.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> This became a problem when the future sales subsequently failed to materialize. Oracle eventually had to restate its earnings twice, and also settled (out of court) <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class-action</a> lawsuits arising from its having overstated its earnings. Ellison stated in 1992 that Oracle had made "an incredible business mistake".<sup id="cite_ref-zdnet200620_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet200620-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Competition" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Informix_Corporation" title="Informix Corporation">Informix</a> overtook <a href="/wiki/Sybase" title="Sybase">Sybase</a> and became Oracle's most important rival. The intense war between Informix CEO Phil White and Ellison made front-page news in <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> for three years. Informix claimed that Oracle had hired away Informix engineers to disclose important trade secrets about an upcoming product. Informix finally dropped its lawsuit against Oracle in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In November 2005, a book detailing the war between Oracle and Informix was published, titled <i>The Real Story of Informix Software and Phil White</i>. It gave a detailed chronology of the battle of Informix against Oracle, and how Informix Software's CEO Phil White landed in jail because of his obsession with overtaking Ellison.
</p><p>Once it had overcome Informix and Sybase, Oracle Corporation enjoyed years of dominance in the database market until use of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a> became widespread in the late 1990s and IBM acquired Informix Software in 2001 (to complement its DB2 database). Today<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Oracle competes for new database licenses on UNIX, Linux, and Windows operating systems primarily against IBM's DB2 and Microsoft SQL Server. IBM's DB2 still<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> dominates the mainframe database market.
</p><p>In 2004, Oracle's sales grew at a rate of 14.5% to $6.2 billion, giving it 41.3% and the top share of the relational-database market (<i>InformationWeek</i> – March 2005), with market share estimated at up to 44.6% in 2005 by some sources.<sup id="cite_ref-Oracle.com_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oracle.com-60">[60]</a></sup>
Oracle Corporation's main competitors in the database arena remain <a href="/wiki/IBM_DB2" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM DB2">IBM DB2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a>, and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Sybase" title="Sybase">Sybase</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teradata" title="Teradata">Teradata</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Oracle.com_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oracle.com-60">[60]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open source</a> databases such as <a href="/wiki/PostgreSQL" title="PostgreSQL">PostgreSQL</a> and <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> also having a significant<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> share of the market. <a href="/wiki/EnterpriseDB" title="EnterpriseDB">EnterpriseDB</a>, based on PostgreSQL, has recently<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> made inroads<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> by proclaiming that its product delivers Oracle compatibility features<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2009)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> at a much lower price-point.
</p><p>In the software-applications market, Oracle Corporation primarily<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> competes against <a href="/wiki/SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="SAP AG">SAP</a>. On March 22, 2007 Oracle sued SAP, accusing them of fraud and unfair competition.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In the market for <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a> software, many other software companies—small and large—have successfully competed in quality with Oracle and SAP products. Business intelligence vendors can be categorized into the "big four" consolidated BI firms such as Oracle, who has entered BI market through a recent trend of acquisitions (including <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_Solutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperion Solutions">Hyperion Solutions</a>), and the independent "pure play" vendors such as <a href="/wiki/MicroStrategy" title="MicroStrategy">MicroStrategy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Actuate_Corporation" title="Actuate Corporation">Actuate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SAS_Institute_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="SAS Institute Inc.">SAS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>Oracle Financials was ranked in the Top 20 Most Popular Accounting Software Infographic by Capterra in 2014, beating out SAP and a number of their other competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oracle_and_SAP">Oracle and SAP</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Oracle and SAP" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>From 1988, Oracle Corporation and the German company <a href="/wiki/SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="SAP AG">SAP AG</a> had a decade-long history of cooperation, beginning with the integration of SAP's <a href="/wiki/SAP_R/3" title="SAP R/3">R/3</a> enterprise application suite with Oracle's relational database products. Despite the SAP partnership with Microsoft, and the increasing integration of SAP applications with Microsoft products (such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a>, a competitor to Oracle Database), Oracle and SAP continue their cooperation. According to Oracle Corporation, the majority of SAP's customers use Oracle databases.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, Oracle began to increase its interest in the enterprise-applications market (in 1989, Oracle had already released Oracle Financials). A series of acquisitions by Oracle Corporation began, most notably with those of <a href="/wiki/PeopleSoft" title="PeopleSoft">PeopleSoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siebel_Systems" title="Siebel Systems">Siebel Systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_Solutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperion Solutions">Hyperion</a>.
</p><p>SAP recognized that Oracle had started to become a competitor in a market where SAP had the <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leadership</a>, and saw an opportunity to lure in customers from those companies that Oracle Corporation had acquired. SAP would offer those customers special discounts on the licenses for its enterprise applications.
</p><p>Oracle Corporation would resort to a similar strategy, by advising SAP customers to get "OFF SAP" (a play on the words of the <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> for its middleware platform "Oracle Fusion for SAP"),<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
and also by providing special discounts on licenses and services to SAP customers who chose Oracle Corporation products.
</p><p>Currently<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Oracle and SAP (the latter through its recently acquired subsidiary <a href="/wiki/TomorrowNow" class="mw-redirect" title="TomorrowNow">TomorrowNow</a>) compete in the third-party enterprise software maintenance and support market. On March 22, 2007, Oracle filed a lawsuit against SAP. In <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation_v._SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Corporation v. SAP AG">Oracle Corporation v. SAP AG</a> Oracle alleged that TomorrowNow, which provides discount support for legacy Oracle product lines, used the accounts of former Oracle customers to systematically download patches and support documents from Oracle's website and to appropriate them for SAP's use.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
Some analysts have suggested the suit could form part of a strategy by Oracle Corporation to decrease competition with SAP in the market for third-party enterprise software maintenance and support.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On July 3, 2007, SAP admitted that TomorrowNow employees had made "inappropriate downloads" from the Oracle support website. However, it claims that SAP personnel and SAP customers had no access to Oracle intellectual property via TomorrowNow. SAP's CEO <a href="/wiki/Henning_Kagermann" title="Henning Kagermann">Henning Kagermann</a> stated that "Even a single inappropriate download is unacceptable from my perspective. We regret very much that this occurred." Additionally, SAP announced that it had "instituted changes" in TomorrowNow's operational oversight.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>On November 23, 2010, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">U.S. district court</a> jury in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a> found that SAP AG must pay Oracle Corp $1.3 billion for copyright infringement, awarding damages that could be the largest-ever for copyright infringement. While admitting liability, SAP estimated the damages at no more than $40 million, while Oracle claimed that they are at least $1.65 billion. The awarded amount is one of the 10 or 20 largest jury verdicts in U.S. legal history. SAP said they were disappointed by the verdict and might appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On September 1, 2011, a federal judge overturned the judgment and offered a reduced amount or a new trial, calling Oracle's original award "grossly" excessive.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Oracle chose a new trial.
</p><p>On August 3, 2012, SAP and Oracle agreed on a judgment for $306 million in damages, pending approval from the U.S. district court judge, “to save time and expense of [a] new trial". After the accord has been approved, Oracle can ask a federal appeals court to reinstate the earlier jury verdict. In addition to the damages payment, SAP has already paid Oracle $120 million for its legal fees.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Slogans">Slogans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Slogans" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li>"Information driven"<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li>For the Oracle Database: "Can't break it, can't break in"<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and "Unbreakable"<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>Enabling the Information Age<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>Enabling the Information Age Through Network Computing"<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>: "The Information Company"<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of 2010: "Software. Hardware. Complete."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of late 2010: "Hardware and Software, Engineered to Work Together"<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li>As of mid 2015: "Integrated Cloud Applications and Platform Services"<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Oracle Corporation produces and distributes the "Oracle ClearView" series of videos as part of its marketing mix.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Trashgate">Trashgate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Trashgate" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Oracle attracted attention from the <a href="/wiki/Computer_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer industry">computer industry</a> and the press after hiring <a href="/wiki/Private_investigator" title="Private investigator">private investigators</a> to dig through the trash of organizations involved in an <a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Microsoft_Corp._(2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="United States v. Microsoft Corp. (2001)">antitrust trial involving Microsoft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The Chairman of Oracle Corporation, Larry Ellison, staunchly defended his company's hiring of an East Coast detective agency to investigate groups that supported rival Microsoft Corporation during its antitrust trial, calling the snooping a "public service". The investigation reportedly included a $1,200 offer to janitors at the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Competitive_Technology" title="Association for Competitive Technology">Association for Competitive Technology</a> to look through Microsoft's trash. When asked how he would feel if others were looking into Oracle's business activities, Ellison said: "We will ship our garbage to Redmond, and they can go through it. We believe in full disclosure."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id=".22Can.27t_break_it.2C_can.27t_break_in.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Can't_break_it,_can't_break_in&quot;">"Can't break it, can't break in"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: &quot;Can't break it, can't break in&quot;" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Oracle Corporation marketed many of its products using the slogan "Can't break it, can't break in", or "Unbreakable".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> This signified a demand on <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a>. Oracle Corporation also stressed the reliability of networked databases and network access to databases as major selling points.
</p><p>However, two weeks after its introduction, <a href="/wiki/David_Litchfield" title="David Litchfield">David Litchfield</a>, Alexander Kornbrust, Cesar Cerrudo and others demonstrated a whole suite of successful attacks against Oracle products.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Oracle Corporation's chief security officer <a href="/wiki/Mary_Ann_Davidson" title="Mary Ann Davidson">Mary Ann Davidson</a> said that, rather than representing a literal claim of Oracle's products' impregnability, she saw the campaign in the context of fourteen independent security evaluations<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> that Oracle Corporation's database server had passed.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_John_Ashcroft">Relationship with John Ashcroft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Relationship with John Ashcroft" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, then-<a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">United States Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Ashcroft" title="John Ashcroft">John Ashcroft</a> sued Oracle Corporation to prevent it from acquiring a multibillion-dollar intelligence contract. After Ashcroft's resignation from government, he founded a lobbying firm, <a href="/wiki/The_Ashcroft_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="The Ashcroft Group">The Ashcroft Group</a>, which Oracle hired in 2005. With the group's help, Oracle went on to acquire the contract.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Expeditionary_Combat_Support_System">Expeditionary Combat Support System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Expeditionary Combat Support System" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Computer_Sciences_Corporation" title="Computer Sciences Corporation">Computer Sciences Corporation</a> reportedly spent a billion dollars developing a computer system for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> that yielded no significant capability, because, according to an Air Force source, the Oracle software on which the system was based could not be adapted to meet the specialized performance criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_Oregon_Healthcare_Exchange">Cover Oregon Healthcare Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cover Oregon Healthcare Exchange" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Oracle Corporation was awarded a contract by the State of Oregon's <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Health_Authority" title="Oregon Health Authority">Oregon Health Authority</a> (OHA) to develop <a href="/wiki/Cover_Oregon" title="Cover Oregon">Cover Oregon</a>, the state's healthcare exchange website, as part of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a>. When the site tried to go live on October 1, 2013, it failed, and registrations had to be taken using paper applications until the site could be fixed.
</p><p>On April 25, 2014, the State of Oregon voted to discontinue Cover Oregon and instead use the federal exchange to enroll Oregon residents.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The cost of switching to the federal portal was estimated at $5 million, whereas fixing Cover Oregon would have required another $78 million.
</p><p>Oracle president <a href="/wiki/Safra_Catz" title="Safra Catz">Safra Catz</a> responded to Cover Oregon and the OHA in a letter claiming that the site's problems were due to OHA mismanagement, specifically that a third-party <a href="/wiki/Systems_integrator" title="Systems integrator">systems integrator</a> was not hired to manage the complex project.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2014, Oracle Corporation sued Cover Oregon for breach of contract,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> and then later that month the state of Oregon sued Oracle Corporation, in a civil complaint for breach of contract, fraud, filing false claims and "<a href="/wiki/Racketeering" class="mw-redirect" title="Racketeering">racketeering</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In September 2016, the two sides reached a settlement valued at over $100 million to the state, and a six-year agreement for Oracle to continue modernizing state software and IT.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Events" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_of_Sun_Microsystems">Acquisition of Sun Microsystems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Acquisition of Sun Microsystems" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sun_acquisition_by_Oracle" title="Sun acquisition by Oracle">Sun acquisition by Oracle</a></div>
<p>On January 27, 2010, Oracle announced it had completed its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>—valued at more than $7 billion—a move that transformed Oracle from solely a software company to a manufacturer of both software and hardware. The acquisition was delayed for several months by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> because of concerns about <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, but was unconditionally approved in the end.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> This acquisition was important to some in the <a href="/wiki/Open_source_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source community">open source community</a> and also to some other companies, as they feared Oracle might end Sun's traditional support of <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open source</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Since the acquisition, Oracle has discontinued <a href="/wiki/OpenSolaris" title="OpenSolaris">OpenSolaris</a> and <a href="/wiki/StarOffice" title="StarOffice">StarOffice</a>, and sued <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> over their newly acquired <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> patents from Sun.<sup id="cite_ref-arsjava_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arsjava-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In September 2011, U.S. State Department Embassy cables were leaked<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a>.  One cable revealed that the U.S. pressured the <a href="/wiki/E.U." class="mw-redirect" title="E.U.">E.U.</a> to allow Oracle to acquire Sun.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice_Department_lawsuit">Justice Department lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Justice Department lawsuit" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On July 29, 2010, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> filed suit against Oracle Corporation alleging fraud. The lawsuit argues that the government received deals inferior to those Oracle gave to its commercial clients. The DoJ added its heft to an already existing whistleblower lawsuit filed by Paul Frascella, who was once senior director of contract services at Oracle.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> It was settled in May 2012<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit_against_Google">Lawsuit against Google</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Lawsuit against Google" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oracle_v._Google" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle v. Google">Oracle v. Google</a></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Background" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Oracle, the plaintiff, bought the Java computer programing language when it acquired <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a> in January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJune2011_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJune2011-113">[113]</a></sup> The Java software includes sets of pre-developed software code in order to accomplish common tasks consistently among programs and apps. The pre-developed code is organized into separate "<a href="/wiki/Package_manager" title="Package manager">packages</a>" which each contain a set of "<a href="/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)" title="Class (computer programming)">classes</a>". Each class contains numerous <a href="/wiki/Method_(computer_programming)" title="Method (computer programming)">methods</a>, which instruct a program or app to do a certain task. Software developers "became accustomed to using Java’s designations at the package, class, and method level".<sup id="cite_ref-Quimbee_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quimbee-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>Oracle and <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> (the defendant) tried to negotiate an agreement for Oracle to license Java to Google, which would have allowed Google to use Java in developing programs for mobile devices using the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>. However, the two companies never reached an agreement. After negotiations failed, Google created its own programming platform, which was based on Java, and contained a mix of 37 copied Java packages and new packages developed by Google.<sup id="cite_ref-Quimbee_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quimbee-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="First_trial">First trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: First trial" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2010, Oracle sued Google for <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> for the use of the 37 Java packages.<sup id="cite_ref-Quimbee_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quimbee-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJune2011_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJune2011-113">[113]</a></sup> The case was handled in <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">U.S. District Court for the Northern District of California</a> and assigned to Judge <a href="/wiki/William_Haskell_Alsup" title="William Haskell Alsup">William H. Alsup</a> (who taught himself how to code computers<sup id="cite_ref-verge_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-115">[115]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJune2011_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJune2011-113">[113]</a></sup> In the lawsuit, Oracle sought between $1.4 billion and $6.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJune2011_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJune2011-113">[113]</a></sup> In June 2011 the judge had to force Google through a judicial order to make public the details about Oracle's claim for damages.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersJune2011_113-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersJune2011-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>
By the end of the first jury trial (the legal dispute would eventually go on to another trial) the arguments made by Oracle's attorneys focused on a Java function called "rangeCheck".</p><blockquote><p>"The argument centered on a function called rangeCheck. Of all the lines of code that Oracle had tested—15 million in total—these were the only ones that were 'literally' copied. Every keystroke, a perfect duplicate." – <i>The Verge</i>, 10/19/17<sup id="cite_ref-verge_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-115">[115]</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Although Google admitted to copying the packages, Judge Alsup found that none of the Java packages were covered under copyright protection, and therefore Google did not infringe.<sup id="cite_ref-Quimbee_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quimbee-114">[114]</a></sup></p><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="First_appeal">First appeal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: First appeal" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>After the case was over, Oracle appealed to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Federal_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit</a> (750 F.3d 1339 (2014)).<sup id="cite_ref-Quimbee_114-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quimbee-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup> On May 9, 2014, the appeals court partially reversed Judge Alsup's decision, finding that Java APIs are copyrightable. API stands for "application programming interface" and are how different computer programs or apps communicate with each other. However, the appeals court also left open the possibility that Google might have a "<a href="/wiki/Fair_use" title="Fair use">fair use</a>" defense.<sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Supreme_Court_petition">Supreme Court petition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Supreme Court petition" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On October 6, 2014, Google filed a petition to appeal to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a>, but the Supreme Court denied the petition.<sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
