<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_trial">Second trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Second trial" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The case was then returned to the U.S. District Court for another trial about Google's fair use defense.<sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup> Oracle sought $9 billion in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-ZDNet_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZDNet-117">[117]</a></sup> In May 2016, the trial jury found that Google's use of Java's APIs was considered fair use.<sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_appeal">Second appeal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Second appeal" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In February 2017, Oracle filed another appeal to the U.S. Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit.<sup id="cite_ref-eff-org_116-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eff-org-116">[116]</a></sup> This time it was asking for a new trial because the District Court "repeatedly undermined Oracle's case", which Oracle argued led the jury to make the wrong decision. According to ZDNet, "For example, it [Oracle] says the court wrongly bought Google's claim that Android was limited to smartphones while Java was for PCs, whereas Oracle contends that Java and Android both compete as platforms for smart TVs, cars, and wearables."<sup id="cite_ref-ZDNet_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZDNet-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinuation_of_OpenSolaris">Discontinuation of OpenSolaris</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Discontinuation of OpenSolaris" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 13, 2010, an internal Oracle memo leaked to the Internet cited plans for ending the <a href="/wiki/OpenSolaris" title="OpenSolaris">OpenSolaris</a> operating system project and community.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> With Oracle planning to develop <a href="/wiki/Solaris_(operating_system)" title="Solaris (operating system)">Solaris</a> only in a closed source fashion, OpenSolaris developers moved to the <a href="/wiki/Illumos" title="Illumos">Illumos</a> and <a href="/wiki/OpenIndiana" title="OpenIndiana">OpenIndiana</a> project, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-Phoronix_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phoronix-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinuation_of_OpenSSO">Discontinuation of OpenSSO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Discontinuation of OpenSSO" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As Oracle completed their acquisition of Sun Microsystems in February 2010, they announced that OpenSSO would no longer be their strategic product.<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwonlinecomopennewsitemOraclekillsOpenSSOExpressForgeRockstepsinhtml_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwonlinecomopennewsitemOraclekillsOpenSSOExpressForgeRockstepsinhtml-120">[120]</a></sup> Shortly after, OpenSSO was forked to <a href="/wiki/OpenAM" title="OpenAM">OpenAM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HttpwwwonlinecomopennewsitemOraclekillsOpenSSOExpressForgeRockstepsinhtml_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HttpwwwonlinecomopennewsitemOraclekillsOpenSSOExpressForgeRockstepsinhtml-120">[120]</a></sup> and will continue to be developed and supported by <a href="/wiki/ForgeRock" title="ForgeRock">ForgeRock</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mark_Hurd_as_president">Mark Hurd as president</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Mark Hurd as president" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On September 6, 2010, Oracle announced that former <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hurd" title="Mark Hurd">Mark Hurd</a> was to replace <a href="/wiki/Charles_Phillips_(businessman)" title="Charles Phillips (businessman)">Charles Phillips</a>, who resigned as Oracle Co-President. In an official statement made by Larry Ellison, Phillips had previously expressed his desire to transition out of the company. Ellison had asked Phillips to stay on through the integration of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In a separate statement regarding the transition, Ellison said "Mark did a brilliant job at HP and I expect he'll do even better at Oracle. There is no executive in the IT world with more relevant experience than Mark."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>On September 7, 2010, HP announced a civil lawsuit against Mark Hurd "to protect HP's trade secrets",<sup id="cite_ref-scribd.com_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scribd.com-123">[123]</a></sup> in response to Oracle hiring Hurd. On September 20, Oracle and HP published a joint press release announcing the resolution of the lawsuit on confidential terms and reaffirming commitment to long-term strategic partnership between the companies.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="OpenOffice.org_issue">OpenOffice.org issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: OpenOffice.org issue" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org" title="OpenOffice.org">OpenOffice.org</a> developers formed <a href="/wiki/The_Document_Foundation" title="The Document Foundation">The Document Foundation</a> and received backing by Google, Novell, Red Hat, and Canonical, as well as some others, but were unable to get Oracle to donate the brand OpenOffice.org, causing a fork in the development of OpenOffice.org with the foundation now developing and promoting <a href="/wiki/LibreOffice" title="LibreOffice">LibreOffice</a>. Oracle expressed no interest in sponsoring the new project and asked the OpenOffice.org developers that started the project to resign from the company due to "conflicts of interest". On November 1, 2010, 33 of the OpenOffice.org developers gave their letters of resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-And_So_The_Exodus_Begins_33_OpenOffice.org_Developers_Leave_Oracle_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-And_So_The_Exodus_Begins_33_OpenOffice.org_Developers_Leave_Oracle-125">[125]</a></sup> On June 1, 2011, Oracle donated OpenOffice.org to the <a href="/wiki/Apache_Software_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Apache Software Foundation">Apache Software Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="HP_and_Oracle_lawsuit">HP and Oracle lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: HP and Oracle lawsuit" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On June 15, 2011, HP filed a lawsuit in California Superior Court in Santa Clara, claiming that Oracle had breached an agreement to support the Itanium microprocessor used in HP's high-end enterprise servers.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Oracle called the lawsuit "an abuse of the judicial process"<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> and said that had it known <a href="/wiki/SAP_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="SAP AG">SAP</a>'s <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9o_Apotheker" title="Léo Apotheker">Léo Apotheker</a> was about to be hired as HP's new CEO, any support for HP's Itanium servers would not have been implied.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p><p>On August 1, 2012, a California judge said in a tentative ruling that Oracle must continue porting its software at no cost until HP discontinues its sales of Itanium-based servers.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> HP was awarded $3 billion in damages against Oracle in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> HP argued Oracle's canceling support damaged HP's Itanium server brand. Oracle has announced it will appeal both the decision and damages.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_corrupt_practices">Foreign corrupt practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Foreign corrupt practices" data-section="46" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 31, 2011, <i>The Wall Street Journal</i> reported that Oracle was being investigated by the Federal Bureau of Investigation for paying bribes to government officials in order to win business in Africa, in contravention of the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Corrupt_Practices_Act" title="Foreign Corrupt Practices Act">Foreign Corrupt Practices Act</a> (FCPA).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="GSA_business_bidding_ban">GSA business bidding ban</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: GSA business bidding ban" data-section="47" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 20, 2012 the US General Services Administration banned Oracle from the most popular portal for bidding on GSA contracts for undisclosed reasons. Oracle has previously used this portal for around four hundred million dollars a year in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Oracle previously settled a lawsuit filed under the <a href="/wiki/False_Claims_Act" title="False Claims Act">False Claims Act</a>, which accused the company of <a href="/wiki/Overbilling" title="Overbilling">overbilling</a> the US government between 1998 and 2006. The 2011 settlement forced Oracle to pay $199.5 million to the <a href="/wiki/General_Services_Administration" title="General Services Administration">General Services Administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: People" data-section="48" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Larry_Ellison" title="Larry Ellison">Larry Ellison</a>: executive chairman and CTO (since September 2014), co-founder of the company, previously CEO (1977–2014),<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-ellison-step-down_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-ellison-step-down-136">[136]</a></sup> previously chairman (1990–2004). He owns 25% of the company.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Safra_Catz" title="Safra Catz">Safra Catz</a>: CEO (since September 2014),<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-ellison-step-down_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-ellison-step-down-136">[136]</a></sup> previously co-president (since 2004) and CFO.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In 2016, she was ranked 10th on <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortune Magazine">Fortune's</a></i> Most Powerful Women list.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Henley" title="Jeff Henley">Jeff Henley</a>: vice chairman (since September 2014), chairman (2004–2014). Previously CFO of Oracle (1991–2004).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Hurd" title="Mark Hurd">Mark Hurd</a>: former CEO (2014–2019),<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-ellison-step-down_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-ellison-step-down-136">[136]</a></sup> previously co-president (since 2010). In 2007, Mark Hurd was ranked No. 16 on <i>Fortune</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s list of the 25 Most Powerful People in Business.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> He died in 2019.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Phillips_(businessman)" title="Charles Phillips (businessman)">Charles Phillips</a>: former co-president and director (2003–2010), replaced by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hurd" title="Mark Hurd">Mark Hurd</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Miner" title="Bob Miner">Bob Miner</a>: co-founder of the company and co-architect of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Database" title="Oracle Database">Oracle Database</a>. Led product design and development for Oracle Database (1977–1992). Spun off a technology group within Oracle in 1992. Oracle board member until 1993.  He died in 1994.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ed_Oates" title="Ed Oates">Ed Oates</a>: co-founder of the company. Retired from Oracle in 1996.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Umang_Gupta" title="Umang Gupta">Umang Gupta</a>: former vice president and general manager (1981–1984). Wrote the first business plan for the company.</li>
<li>Bruce Scott: The first hired employee (after the co-founders, employee number 4) at Oracle (then Software Development Laboratories). Scott served as the co-author and co-architect of the Oracle database up to Version 3.  He left Oracle in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Offices" data-section="49" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>Oracle Corporation has its overall headquarters on the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Peninsula" title="San Francisco Peninsula">San Francisco Peninsula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Redwood_Shores,_California" title="Redwood Shores, California">Redwood Shores</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Redwood_City,_California" title="Redwood City, California">Redwood City</a>, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Belmont,_California" title="Belmont, California">Belmont</a> and near <a href="/wiki/San_Carlos_Airport_(California)" title="San Carlos Airport (California)">San Carlos Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA airport code</a>: SQL).
</p><p>Oracle HQ stands on the former site of <a href="/wiki/Marine_World/Africa_USA" title="Marine World/Africa USA">Marine World/Africa USA</a>, which moved from Redwood Shores to <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">Vallejo</a> in 1986. Oracle Corporation originally leased two buildings on the site, moving its finance and administration departments from the corporation's former headquarters on Davis Drive, <a href="/wiki/Belmont,_California" title="Belmont, California">Belmont, California</a>. Eventually, Oracle purchased the complex and constructed a further four main buildings.
</p><p>The distinctive Oracle Parkway buildings, nicknamed the Emerald City,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> served as sets for the futuristic headquarters of the fictional company "NorthAm Robotics" in the <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Bicentennial_Man_(film)" title="Bicentennial Man (film)">Bicentennial Man</a></i> (1999).<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
The campus represented the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Cyberdyne_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyberdyne Systems">Cyberdyne Systems</a> in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator_Genisys" title="Terminator Genisys">Terminator Genisys</a></i> (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1208px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Oracle headquarters in Redwood Shores, California."><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg/1200px-Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1200" height="300" data-file-width="16000" data-file-height="4000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 1200px;height: 300px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg/1200px-Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="1200" data-height="300"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oracle_Redwood_City_February_2013_panorama.jpg" title="File:Oracle Redwood City February 2013 panorama.jpg"> </a></div>Oracle headquarters in Redwood Shores, California.</div></div></div>

</ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structures">Corporate structures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Corporate structures" data-section="50" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>Oracle Corporation operates in multiple markets and has acquired several companies which formerly functioned autonomously. In some cases these provided the starting points for global business units (GBUs) targeting particular vertical markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Sanati-18Dec2017_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanati-18Dec2017-144">[144]</a></sup> Oracle Corporation GBUs include:
</p>
<ul><li>Communications</li>
<li>Construction and engineering - formerly the Primavera GBU</li>
<li>Financial services</li>
<li>Food and Beverages</li>
<li>Health sciences</li>
<li>Hospitality</li>
<li>Retail</li>
<li>Utilities</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Sponsorships" data-section="51" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg/220px-German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg/220px-German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_Sailing_Grand_Prix_2006_Oracle-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BMW Oracle Racing USA-71, at the German Sailing Grand Prix Kiel 2006. It was moored at Oracle headquarters in Redwood Shores, California until 2014.</div></div></div>
<p>On October 20, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> and the Oracle Corporation announced a 10-year agreement in which the Oakland Arena would become known as the <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Arena">Oracle Arena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>Larry Ellison's sailing team competes as <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Team_USA" title="Oracle Team USA">Oracle Team USA</a>. The team has won the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America's Cup">America's Cup</a> twice, in 2010 (as BMW Oracle Racing)<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> and in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> despite being penalized for cheating.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Sean_D._Tucker" title="Sean D. Tucker">Sean Tucker</a>'s "Challenger II" stunt biplane is sponsored by Oracle and performs frequently at air shows around the US.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>On January 9, 2019, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> reported that the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> entered into a 20-year agreement to rename their stadium <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Park" title="Oracle Park">Oracle Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oracle_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="52" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">

<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On July 3, 2007, SAP admitted that TomorrowNow employees had made "inappropriate downloads" from the Oracle support web site. <li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a href="/wiki/Monty_Widenius" class="mw-redirect" title="Monty Widenius">Widenius, Monty</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.helpmysql.org">"Save MySQL!"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. MySQL itself remains licensed under the GPL.
